Jamison Brereton

109 (821)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Dhiс╣гс╣Зya Fires, descendants of ─к┼Ыvara
22 verses: dvipad─Б vir─Бj, arranged in trcas ╠е
The Anukramaс╣З─лтАЩs fanciful ascription of this hymn to the dhiс╣гс╣Зya (тАЬholyтАЭ) fires finds no echo in the composition itself.
The lightness and brevity of this meter (each verse containing four p─Бdas of a mere five syllables each) do not lend themselves to complex phraseology or elaborate images. Instead the hymn consists primarily of standard apostrophes to Soma (e.g., the imperative тАЬpurify yourselfтАЭ occurs five times in the hymn: vss. 4, 5, 6, 7, 10) and simple present-tense descriptions of the process of preparation (e.g., vs. 11 тАЬthey purifyтАЭ; vs. 12 тАЬthey groomтАЭ).
For links with the next hymn, see the introduction to IX.110.

English translation:

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself, o Soma, possessing heavenly brilliance and good streams, along the (fleece) of the sheep as the great ancient one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The morphological identity of mah─Б╠Бm is uncertain: it could be acc. sg. (m.) (see AiG III.251, etc.) or gen. pl. to m├бh- (so Grassmann) - or, in my opinion, nom. sg. masc.

to mah─Б╠Бnt-. Most (Oldenberg, Geldner, Renou, Lubotsky) take it as an acc., supplying тАШfleeceтАЩ or тАШbackтАЩ, hence тАЬalong the great (fleece) of the sheep.тАЭ For detailed disc. see Oldenberg ad loc. and ad II.24.11. Although this is certainly possible, the filter is not usually so described.

A similar problem arises with a gen. pl. interpr., acdg. to which it would modify ├бv─лn─Бmi тАЬof the great sheep.тАЭ Since the most likely entity to be called тАШgreatтАЩ in this vs. is Soma (cf., e.g., mah─Б╠Бn samudr├бс╕е in vs. 4, I think it likely that the form is nom. sg. In this sandhi position (before vowel) we would expect mah─Б╠Бm╠Р(cf., e.g., IX.66.16 mah─Б╠Бm╠Рasi), but I suggest that the anun─Бsika was redactionally changed to m because the form was reinterp. as a gen. pl. modifying immed. following ├бv─лn─Бm.

English translation:

тАЬMay, the Soma regulated by the priests, engendered, purified, exhilarating, all-knowing bring us all (riches).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Being guided by men after being born purified, he streams all (goods) [/to all (domains)]тАФthe gladdening one who finds the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is not certain how to construe v├н┼Ыv─Бni with kс╣гarat, and how this is decided will also determine what to supply with the adj. Forms of тИЪkс╣гar тАШstreamтАЩ without preverb generally do not take an obj. or an Inhaltsakk. (though cf. IX.35.3, 61.3, 86.37 for the latter), though it is found with an acc. of goal or extent of space (e.g., IX.33.2, 63.14). In vss. 16, 17 in this hymn, akс╣г─Бс╕е has intrans. value, though in vs. 16 with accusatives of the space traversed. If we take the verb in that sense, v├н┼Ыv─Бni could pick up v├н┼Ыv─Б тАж dh─Б╠Бma in vs. 4, with the sense тАЬstream to/across all (domains).тАЭ However, the phrase v├н┼Ыv─Бni dr├бviс╣З─Бni тАЬall goodsтАЭ might give us pause, and suggest that kс╣г├бrat here takes an Inhaltsakk., тАЬstream all (goods).тАЭ There is no way to decide, and both may be meant. Geldner, Renou, and Hoffmann (123) all opt for the latter.

Extolling the gods: praj─Бm is separated from ur─Бс╣Зaс╕е;

Jamison Brereton

The drop being purified, being chosen, will make offspring and all goods for us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In all clear cases ur─Бс╣З├б- is passive, тАШbeing chosenтАЩ (see comm. ad IV.6.3).

Grassmann, Geldner, and Renou all take it as trans. with praj─Б╠Бm as obj., but there is no reason why this acc. canтАЩt be taken as an obj. of k├бrat, parallel to v├н┼Ыv─Бni dr├бvaс╣З─Бni.

k├бrat opening the 2nd hemistich rhymes with kс╣г├бrat in the same position in vs. 8. Nonetheless they are morphologically divergent, with k├бrat a subjunctive and kс╣г├бrat an injunc. Despite their parallelism kс╣г├бrat is unlikely to have modal value anticipating k├бrat; Hoffmann (123 and n. 26) convincingly takes kс╣г├бrat in тАЬgeneralтАЭ sense.

Jamison Brereton

He bears the name dear to Indra, with which he smashes all
obstacles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. presents a double ambiguity. On the one hand c─Б╠Бru ├нndrasya n─Б╠Бma can mean either тАЬthe dear name of IndraтАЭ (as Geldner/Renou take it) or тАЬthe name dear to IndraтАЭ; the question is whether the name Soma bears is тАЬIndra,тАЭ as the first alternative implies, or тАЬSoma,тАЭ with the second. I prefer the second, since constructing a plausible reason why Soma would be called Indra is difficult: GeldnerтАЩs (n.

  1. тАЬer wirkt in Indra and f├╝hrt so dessen NamenтАЭ doesnтАЩt seem sufficient to me.

The second ambiguity is located in the 2nd hemistich and has two parts: what/who is the referent of y├йna and who is the subj. of jagh─Б╠Бna? The Geldner/Renou interpr.

seems to take the referent of y├йna to be тАЬthe name IndraтАЭ and the subj. of the verb to be Soma (though neither is explicit about it). I recognize that this would be a pleasing paradox, since Indra is the default agent in this formula. But I wonder if instead Indra is the subj. of his signature verb, and y├йna refers to soma, with the name equivalent to the substance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Vss. 16 and 17 contain the sequence akс╣г─Бс╕е sah├бsra(-dh─Бraс╕е / -retaс╕е) in the same position in the vs. All 3 vss. concern SomaтАЩs journey. The various phrases with agentive instr. in 17 and 18 reprise and reshuffle those in 15: g├│bhiс╕е ┼Ыr─лt├бsya (15) is echoed by g├│bhiс╕е ┼Ыr─лс╣З─Бnaс╕е (17); nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е sut├бsya (15) gets divided and refitted into two phrases, nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е yem─Бn├бс╕е and ├бdribhiс╕е sut├бс╕е (18).

English translation:

тАЬIndu is effused for Indra’s, is effused downward– fierce, mixing (with the milk), flowing (into) the water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Prerayam = stimulating (Indra);

To┼Ыate = hanyate, is beaten, abhiс╣г┼лyate, is effused

Jamison Brereton

The drop spills, spills down for IndraтАФthe mighty one preparing and setting the waters to flow.

Jamison Brereton Notes

An extra vs. in a different meter. Oldenberg suggests either 12 8 or 8 4 8, Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition either 12 8 or 8 12. Although the opening of the vs. contains 5 syllables and could therefore be a Dvipada Vir─Бj p─Бda, the following finite verb to┼Ыate is unaccented and cannot start a new p─Бda.

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрдиреНрджреБрдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдХрдГ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп) рдХрд░реНрдордпреЛрдЧрд┐рдиреЗ (рддреЛрд╢рддреЗ) рд╕рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╛рддреНрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдГ) рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд░реВрдкрдГ рд╕рдГ (рд╢реНрд░реАрдгрдиреН) рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрдиреН (рдЕрдкрдГ, рд░рд┐рдгрдиреН) рдордиреНрджрдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдпрдкрдирдпрдиреН (рдирд┐, рддреЛрд╢рддреЗ) рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдирд╛рд╢рдпрддрд┐реереиреирее рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд╡реЛрддреНрддрд░рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореЗрдХреЛрдирд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГрее
